The Transmission and Authorship of Fiqh al-Akbar
Explains the attribution and transmission of Fiqh al-Akbar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Fiqh al-Akbar was transmitted from Imam Abu Hanifa through his students and later scholars, and why attributing it to him is correct despite being compiled by others.

Core Idea
Fiqh al-Akbar is Abu Hanifa's dictation, compiled by students.

This lesson explores the chain of transmission of one of the most important texts in Hanafi theology. The passage clarifies that while Imam Abu Hanifa did not personally write down his teachings, his dictations were collected by his companions and passed down through a sound chain to Imam Abu Mansur al-Maturidi. Understanding this process helps us appreciate the reliability of the text and the careful methodology of early scholars.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the full translation. Let the author's description of the transmission process sink in.
Notice the chain of names—from Abu Hanifa to al-Maturidi.
2
Identify the key figures and roles
List the companions who received dictation (Hammad, Abu Yusuf, etc.) and the later compilers (Ismail ibn Hammad, etc.). Note the dual role of Abu Mutii al-Balkhi as both recipient and collector.
The passage gives two correct attributions depending on perspective.
3
Understand the dual attribution
The author says attributing to Abu Hanifa is correct because content is his dictation, and attributing to Abu Mutii is also correct because he compiled it. Grasp this nuance.
This is like the Musnad of al-Shafi'i, compiled by someone else.
4
Reflect on the analogy
Consider how the Musnad of al-Shafi'i, though compiled by Abu al-Abbas al-Asamm, is still attributed to al-Shafi'i. This strengthens the point that compilation does not negate authorship.
Analogy helps understand the Hanafi case.
5
Draw the lesson
Conclude that even without Abu Hanifa writing, his teachings are preserved reliably. This explains why Fiqh al-Akbar is a foundational text.
The chain is sound (isnad sahih) to al-Maturidi.

فقه الأكبر تصنيف حضرة الإمام الأعظم أبي حنيفة رضي الله تعالى عنه. وقد عُلم مما تقدم أن هذه الكتب من تأليف الإمام نفسه والصحيح أن هذه المسائل المذكورة في هذه الكتب من أمالي الإمام التي أملاها على أصحابه كحماد وأبي يوسف وأبي مطيع الحكم بن عبد الله البلخي وأبي مقاتل حفص بن مسلم السمرقندي من الأئمة عنهم فمنهم الذين قاموا بجمعها وتلقاها جماعة كإسماعيل بن حماد حفيد الإمام ومحمد بن مقاتل الرازي ومحمد بن سماعة ونصير بن يحيى البلخي وشداد بن الحكم وغيرهم إلى أن وصلت بالإسناد الصحيح إلى الإمام أبي منصور الماتريدي، فمن عزاهن إلى الإمام صح لكون تلك المسائل من إملائه ومن عزاهن إلى أبي مطيع البلخي أو غيره ممن هو في طبقته أو ممن هو بعدهم صح، لكونها من جمعه ونظير ذلك المسند المنسوب للإمام الشافعي فإنه من تخريج أبي عمرو محمد بن جعفر بن محمد بن مطر النيسابوري أبي العباس الأصم من أصول الشافعي ويرجح كثير من العلماء أن تلاميذ أبي حنيفة تلقوا عنه الأخبار والفقه ودونوها وقاموا بتبويبها ومن ذلك كتاب الآثار لأبي يوسف وكتاب الآثار لمحمد بن الحسن وإن كان أبو حنيفة لم يدون بنفسه شيئًا من محتويات هذه الكتب إلا أنها من فقهه وأخباره
Fiqh al-Akbar is the composition of the presence of the Greatest Imam Abu Hanifa, may Allah be pleased with him. And it has been known from what preceded that these books are from the authorship of the Imam himself, and the correct view is that these issues mentioned in these books are from the dictations (amali) of the Imam which he dictated to his companions, such as Hammad, Abu Yusuf, Abu Mutii al-Hakam ibn Abd Allah al-Balkhi, and Abu Muqatil Hafs ibn Muslim al-Samarqandi, from the imams, may Allah be pleased with them, and among them are those who undertook their collection. And a group received them, such as Ismail ibn Hammad, the grandson of the Imam, Muhammad ibn Muqatil al-Razi, Muhammad ibn Samaa, Nusayr ibn Yahya al-Balkhi, Shaddad ibn al-Hakam, and others, until they reached by sound chain of transmission (isnad) to Imam Abu Mansur al-Maturidi. So whoever attributes them to the Imam is correct because those issues are from his dictation, and whoever attributes them to Abu Mutii al-Balkhi or others of his rank or after them is correct because they are from his collection. And analogous to that is the Musnad attributed to Imam al-Shafi'i, for it is from the extraction of Abu Amr Muhammad ibn Jafar ibn Muhammad ibn Matar al-Naysaburi, Abu al-Abbas al-Asamm, from the sources of al-Shafi'i. And many scholars prefer that the students of Abu Hanifa received from him reports and jurisprudence, recorded them, and undertook their classification. Among that is the Kitab al-Athar of Abu Yusuf and the Kitab al-Athar of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, even if Abu Hanifa did not personally record anything from the contents of these books, they are from his jurisprudence and reports.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the attribution and transmission of the book Fiqh al-Akbar. It begins by stating that Fiqh al-Akbar is the composition of Imam Abu Hanifa. The author clarifies that the correct view is that the issues in this book come from Imam Abu Hanifa's dictation to his students, including Hammad, Abu Yusuf, Abu Mutii al-Balkhi, and Abu Muqatil al-Samarqandi. These students or later scholars collected and transmitted them. The chain of transmission reached Imam Abu Mansur al-Maturidi through a sound isnad. The author then notes that whether one attributes the text directly to Imam Abu Hanifa or to Abu Mutii al-Balkhi (or other collectors) is valid, as in the first case the content is from the Imam's dictation, and in the second case the collection is done by them. He draws an analogy with the Musnad of al-Shafi'i, which was compiled by Abu al-Abbas al-Asamm from al-Shafi'i's materials. Finally, he mentions that many scholars hold that Abu Hanifa's students received his fiqh and hadith, wrote them down, and arranged them, giving examples like the Kitab al-Athar of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad ibn al-Hasan. Even though Abu Hanifa did not personally write any of these books, they are still considered his fiqh and reports.

Key Terms
أمالي
إسناد
أبو منصور الماتريدي
فقه الأكبر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Fiqh al-Akbar was written directly by Abu Hanifa.
Correction: It was actually dictated by him and compiled by his students.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the correct view about the authorship of Fiqh al-Akbar?
A) It was written entirely by Imam Abu Hanifa himself.
B) It consists of dictations from Imam Abu Hanifa collected by his students.
C) It was written by Abu Mansur al-Maturidi.
D) It was written by Abu Mutii al-Balkhi without any input from Abu Hanifa.

Key Takeaway
Fiqh al-Akbar is authentically from Imam Abu Hanifa through his dictations, compiled by his students, and transmitted via a sound chain to Imam al-Maturidi.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The scholars who transmitted Fiqh al-Akbar ensured it reached us through a sound chain. How carefully do you verify the sources of your own religious knowledge? Will you commit to learning from those with a solid chain of learning?
?
Abu Hanifa's students dedicated themselves to recording his dictations. What are you doing to preserve the Islamic knowledge you have been given for the next generation? Can you name one thing you will actively pass on?
?
This passage shows that even though Abu Hanifa did not write the book himself, his teachings are authentically preserved. Do you value the content of what you learn over the form? Or do you sometimes dismiss a teaching because it wasn't delivered in a certain way? Challenge yourself to focus on the essence.

Classification of creedal matters by epistemic source
Ali al-Qari classifies creedal matters into three categories based on epistemic source.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three epistemic sources of creedal matters and why some require revelation.

Core Idea
Creedal matters are known by reason, revelation, or both.

This passage from Ali al-Qari’s commentary presents a foundational classification in Islamic theology: how we come to know creedal truths. It distinguishes matters known by reason alone, revelation alone, and both. Understanding this classification helps clarify the roles of intellect and scripture in Islamic belief.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse. Then read the translation. Let the classification structure emerge naturally.
Notice that the author uses 'منها' to list categories.
2
Identify the three categories
The passage presents three categories of creedal matters based on epistemic source. Find each one and note the examples given for each.
The categories are: reason alone, revelation alone, and both.
3
Understand the argument for reason alone
The author argues that matters like the existence of a Creator cannot be proven by revelation alone because that would be circular (revelation depends on the Messenger's truth). Think about why this is a strong argument.
Circular reasoning is a logical fallacy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسائل الاعتقاد منها ما يدرك بالعقل وحده كقولنا: إن للعالم صانعاً وله كلاماً، والرسول حق، إذ لو أثبت أمثال هذا بالسمع لدار ومنها ما يدرك بالسمع وحده كحشر الأجساد والثواب والعقاب في المعاد، ومنها ما يدرك بكل كتوحيد الله تعالى (المعتمد المستند، ص ١٤)
Matters of belief: among them are those perceived by reason alone, like our statement: the world has a Maker, He has speech, and the Messenger is true, for if one were to prove such things by revelation, it would become circular; and among them are those perceived by revelation alone, like the gathering of bodies and reward and punishment in the hereafter; and among them are those perceived by both, like the tawhid (unification) of Allah, the Most High (al-Mu'tamad al-Mustanad, p. 14).
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage classifies creedal matters into three categories based on the source of knowledge. First are matters known by reason alone, such as the existence of a Creator, that He has speech, and that the Messenger is true. The author argues that proving these by revelation would be circular (since revelation itself depends on the Messenger's truthfulness). Second are matters known by revelation alone, such as bodily resurrection and reward/punishment in the afterlife, which reason cannot determine. Third are matters known by both reason and revelation, such as the oneness of Allah (tawhid). The source citation indicates this is from al-Mu'tamad al-Mustanad.

Key Terms
عقل
سمع
توحيد
معاد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that all creedal matters can be proven by reason alone.
Correction: This passage shows that some matters, like bodily resurrection, are known only through revelation.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which type of creedal matter is known by both reason and revelation?
A) The existence of a Creator
B) The truth of the Messenger
C) The tawhid of Allah
D) Bodily resurrection

Key Takeaway
Creedal matters are classified based on epistemic source: reason alone, revelation alone, or both.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
How many of your beliefs about Allah, the Prophet, or the afterlife have you accepted without ever interrogating whether they are based on reason or revelation? Which category does your certainty about tawhid fall into, and what does that demand of you in terms of study?
?
Examine your heart: have you ever relied on a circular justification for your faith—believing something simply because it is in the Qur'an without also considering the rational foundation that makes the Qur'an authoritative? What step have you taken to personally verify that foundation?
?
If some matters of belief can only be known through revelation (like bodily resurrection), how does that affect your attitude towards learning the Qur'an and Sunnah? Do you treat these revealed matters with the same intellectual seriousness as the rational proofs, or do you neglect them because they seem 'less rational'?

The Nobility of Tawheed and Its Condition
Ali al-Qari opens his commentary with praise and defines the condition for tawheed's nobility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the science of tawheed is considered the noblest science only when it remains bound to the Quran, Sunnah, and consensus, and does not rely solely on rational arguments.

Core Idea
Tawheed's nobility depends on staying within revelation, not on pure reason.

This opening passage from Sharh al-Fiqh al-Akbar establishes the foundational principle for the entire study of tawheed. The author, Ali al-Qari, immediately sets the rule: the science of tawheed is the most honored of sciences, but only if it remains anchored in the revealed sources. He warns against the error of those who built their theology on purely rational arguments, thereby leaving the path of Ahl al-Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening praises
Notice how the author begins with tasmiyah, hamd, and salawat, setting a tone of reverence. This reflects the Islamic etiquette of beginning any worthy work.
The attributes of Allah mentioned here (First, Last, etc.) are key tawheed concepts.
2
Identify the main claim
The author states that 'the science of tawheed is the noblest of sciences in accordance with the object known.' What does he mean by 'object known'? It refers to Allah, the Most Noble.
3
Find the condition
The nobility is immediately qualified: 'but on condition that it does not depart from the meaning of the Book, the Sunnah, and the consensus of the upright.' This is the central point.
The 'upright' are the reliable scholars of Ahl al-Sunnah.
4
Understand the warning
The author contrasts this with the people of innovation who admitted purely rational arguments, leading them to abandon the straight path. This sets up the methodology of the book.
Rational arguments ('aql) are not rejected entirely, but they must be subservient to revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شرح الفقه الأكبر
مقدمة الشيخ على القاري
بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم
الحمد لله رب الوجود، ذي الكرم والفضل والجود الأول القديم بلا ابتداء، والآخر الكريم بلا انتهاء، لم يزل ولا يزال صاحب نعوت الكمال من صفات الجلال والجمال، المنزه عن سمات النقصان والحدوث والزوال والصلاة والسلام على أكمل مظاهر الحق في مرأى الخلق، نبي الرحمة وشفيع الأمة، وعلى آله وأصحابه الطيبين الطاهرين وعلى أتباعه وأشياعه إلى يوم الدين.
أما بعد فيقول أفقر العباد إلى بر ربه الباري علي بن سلطان محمد القاري عاملهما الله بلطفه الخفي وكرمه الوفي : اعلم أن علم التوحيد الذي هو أساس بناء التأييد، أشرف العلوم تبعاً للمعلوم لكن بشرط أن لا يخرج من مدلول الكتاب والسنة وإجماع العدول، ولا يدخل فيه مداخل مجردة لأدلة العقول كما وقع فيه أهل البدعة فتركوا طريق الجادة التي عليها أهل السنة والجماعة.
Commentary on the Greatest Fiqh
Introduction of Sheikh Ali al-Qari
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful.
Praise be to Allah, the Lord of existence, Possessor of generosity, bounty, and munificence, the First, the Eternal without beginning, and the Last, the Generous without end. He has never ceased and will never cease to possess attributes of perfection from the attributes of majesty and beauty, transcendent above all characteristics of deficiency, temporality, and annihilation. Blessings and peace be upon the most perfect manifestation of truth in the sight of creation, the Prophet of mercy and intercessor of the nation, and upon his family and his pure and upright companions, and upon his followers and partisans until the Day of Judgment.
To proceed: The poorest of servants to the goodness of his Lord, the Creator, Ali ibn Sultan Muhammad al-Qari – may Allah deal with both of them with His subtle grace and abundant generosity – says: Know that the science of tawheed, which is the foundation of the edifice of confirmation, is the noblest of sciences in accordance with the object known, but on condition that it does not depart from the meaning of the Book, the Sunnah, and the consensus of the upright, nor admit purely rational arguments as the people of innovation did, so they abandoned the straight path upon which the People of the Sunnah and the Community are.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage is the opening of the book. It begins with the basmala, hamd, and salawat, establishing the theological framework. Then the author, Ali al-Qari, introduces the subject: the science of tawheed. He declares it the noblest of sciences, but immediately qualifies that this nobility is conditional: it must adhere to the Quran, Sunnah, and scholarly consensus, and must not rely solely on rational arguments, as the people of innovation did. This sets the tone for the whole work — a defense of orthodox Sunni kalam as grounded in revelation, distinguished from speculative theology that deviates.

Key Terms
علم التوحيد
أهل السنة والجماعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the science of kalam (theology) is purely rational and independent of revelation.
Correction: The author clarifies that tawheed's nobility is conditional: it must not depart from the Book, Sunnah, and consensus, and must not rely solely on rational arguments.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the condition for the science of tawheed to be the noblest science?
A) It must be studied in Arabic.
B) It must not depart from the Quran, Sunnah, and consensus.
C) It must use only rational arguments.
D) It must be taught by a sheikh.

Key Takeaway
The science of tawheed is the noblest of sciences, but only when it is firmly rooted in the Quran, Sunnah, and scholarly consensus, avoiding reliance on pure reason alone.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Qari warns that admitting purely rational arguments into tawheed leads to abandoning the straight path. When you encounter a theological question that seems logically compelling but contradicts a clear text, do you trust your reason or the revelation? What is at stake in that choice?
?
The nobility of tawheed is conditional on staying within the Quran, Sunnah, and scholarly consensus. Have you ever been tempted to prefer an opinion that felt 'more rational' than what the scholars of Ahl al-Sunnah have agreed upon? How can you cultivate humility before the transmitted sources?
?
The people of innovation left the path because they relied on their own reasoning. In your own study of Islam, are there areas where you rely more on your logic than on the teachings of the pious predecessors? What practical step can you take today to align your approach with the method of Ahl al-Sunnah?

Early Scholars' Disapproval of Kalam
Historical account of early scholars' condemnation of kalam with quotes and fatwas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the strong condemnations of kalam by early scholars were directed at a blameworthy type of speculative theology, not at the rational defense of faith (praiseworthy kalam).

Core Idea
Early scholars condemned blameworthy kalam, not all rational theology.

This passage contains powerful statements from early Islamic authorities—Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam al-Shafi'i—that seem to reject the science of kalam entirely. Yet, the author of this very book is writing a work of kalam. This paradox invites us to read carefully: the condemnations target a specific, blameworthy form of kalam that contradicts scripture and leads to heresy. As we go through the text, we will see how the author himself distinguishes between what is condemned and what is praiseworthy.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its full translation. Notice the strong language used by Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i. Do not jump to conclusions yet—just absorb the text.
The passage includes several separate quotes; pay attention to each one.
2
Analyze Abu Yusuf's paradoxical saying
Abu Yusuf says: 'Knowledge of kalam is ignorance, and ignorance of it is knowledge.' The commentary offers two interpretations. Try to understand both: (1) believing kalam to be invalid is beneficial knowledge, (2) turning away from it protects one's intellect.
This shows that even the strictest condemnation allows for a nuanced understanding.
3
Study al-Shafi'i's ruling
Al-Shafi'i prescribes physical punishment and public humiliation for people of kalam. Note that he explicitly ties this to those who 'abandon the Book and the Sunnah.' This is key: the condemnation is conditional.
Also note his statement that all sciences besides Quran, hadith, and fiqh are a distraction.
4
Consider the fatwas and context
The passage ends with fatwas excluding mutakallimun from bequests to scholars and ordering the sale of kalam books. Ask yourself: why would the author include these harsh views if he himself writes kalam? The answer is that he distinguishes between praiseworthy and blameworthy kalam.
The author's own work is a defense of orthodox creed, so he rejects only the deviant forms.
5
Reflect on the purpose of this lesson
Now step back. The learning objective is to see that the early scholars' disapproval was specific. Use the passage to understand the gravity of deviant kalam, but also note the door left open for legitimate theological discourse.
This prepares you to appreciate subsequent discussions that define the proper limits of kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما ما وقع من كراهة أكثر السلف وجمع من الخلف ومنعهم من علم الكلام وما يتبعه من المنطق وما يقربه من المرام حتى قال الإمام أبو يوسف رحمه الله لبشر المريسي: «العلم بالكلام هو الجهل والجهل بالكلام هو العلم». وكأنه أراد بالجهل به اعتقاد عدم صحته، فإن ذلك علم نافع، أو أراد به الإعراض عنه وترك الإلتفات إلى اعتباره، فإن ذلك يصون علم الرجل وعقله فيكون علما بهذا الاعتبار. وعنه أيضاً : من طلب العلم بالكلام تزندق ومن طلب المال بالكيمياء أفلس ومن طلب غريب الحديث فقد كذب». وقال الإمام الشافعي رحمه الله: «حكمي أهل الكلام أن يضربوا بالجريد والنعال ويطاف بهم في العشائر والقبائل ويقال هذا جزاء من ترك الكتاب والسنة وأقبل على كلام أهل البدعة». وقال أيضاً:
ومن كل العلوم سوى القرآن مشغلة إلا الحديث وإلا الفقه في الدين العلم ما كان فيه "قال حدثنا" وما سوى ذلك وسواس الشياطين كلامه أيضاً: «لأن يلقى الله العبد بكل ذنب خلا الشرك خير له من أن يلقاه بشيء من علم الكلام». وقال: «لقد اطلعت من أهل الكلام على شيء ما ظننت مسلماً يقوله». وذكر أصحابنا في الفتاوى «أنه لو أوصى لعلماء بلده لا يدخل المتكلمون ولو أوصى إنسان أن يوقف من كتبه ما هو من كتب العلم فأفتى السلف أنه يباع ما فيها من كتب الكلام».
As for what occurred of dislike from most of the early generations and a group of later generations, and their prohibition of the science of kalam and what follows it of logic and what brings it close to the goal, until Imam Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him, said to Bishr al-Marisi: 'Knowledge of kalam is ignorance, and ignorance of it is knowledge.' It seems that he meant by ignorance of it the belief in its invalidity, for that is beneficial knowledge, or he meant turning away from it and not paying attention to its consideration, for that protects one's knowledge and intellect, so it becomes knowledge in this respect. Also from him: 'He who seeks knowledge through kalam becomes a heretic (zindiq), he who seeks wealth through alchemy becomes bankrupt, and he who seeks rare hadith lies.' And Imam al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, said: 'My ruling regarding the people of kalam is that they should be beaten with palm branches and sandals, and be paraded among the tribes and clans, and it should be said: "This is the punishment for those who abandon the Book and the Sunnah and turn to the speech of the people of innovation."' He also said: 'All sciences besides the Quran are a distraction, except for hadith and fiqh in religion. The (true) knowledge is that which contains "he said: we were told", and anything other than that is the whispering of devils.' And also his saying: 'For a servant to meet Allah with every sin except shirk is better for him than to meet Him with anything from the science of kalam.' And he said: 'I have seen from the people of kalam something I did not think a Muslim would say.' And our companions mentioned in the fatwas: 'If someone bequeaths to the scholars of his town, the mutakallimun (theologians) are not included. And if someone wills that his books which are from the books of knowledge be endowed (waqf), the early generations gave the verdict that what is in it of books of kalam should be sold.'
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage discusses the early Islamic disapproval of speculative theology (kalam). The author acknowledges that many early and later scholars disliked kalam, and he provides strong statements from Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i. Abu Yusuf's paradoxical saying that 'knowledge of kalam is ignorance' is explained as either a condemnation of false kalam or a commendation of avoiding it. Al-Shafi'i's harsh ruling prescribes physical punishment and public humiliation for those who engage in kalam, calling it a distraction. The author includes these accounts to show the gravity of deviating from transmitted knowledge. However, the context of the book shows that the author himself is writing a kalam work, so he distinguishes between praiseworthy and blameworthy kalam. The passage ends with a fatwa excluding mutakallimun from bequests to scholars and ordering the sale of books of kalam, indicating the severity of the early stance.

Key Terms
علم الكلام
الجهل
التزندق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Kalam is completely forbidden in Islam without exception.
Correction: Early scholars condemned only blameworthy kalam that contradicts the Quran and Sunnah; praiseworthy kalam that defends orthodox creed is permitted and engaged in by the author of this book.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what did Imam al-Shafi'i rule regarding the people of kalam?
A) They should be given a warning.
B) They should be beaten and paraded.
C) They should be debated.
D) They should be ignored.

Key Takeaway
The early scholars' harsh words against kalam were directed at speculative theology that opposes the Quran and Sunnah, not at the rational defense of faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever rejected a method of seeking knowledge simply because it was criticized in public discourse, without examining its actual intention? This lesson shows that even harsh condemnations have specific targets. How can you avoid overgeneralizing in your own judgments about scholarly pursuits? What step will you take to investigate before dismissing?
?
The author of this lesson engages in kalam despite reporting strong condemnations from the imams. Are you willing to study matters that may be misunderstood or misrepresented by others? What does your answer reveal about your commitment to truth over social approval? Name one such area in your life where you need courage to pursue deeper understanding.
?
Abu Yusuf said, 'Ignorance of kalam is knowledge.' In what area of your faith might it be better for you to remain in simple submission rather than delve into argumentation? Contrast that with an area where you must seek clarity through rational study. What is the difference, and how will you decide which approach to take?

The Single Scholar as the Community
Sufyan's saying that a single jurist on a mountain is the community.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a single scholar of truth can be considered equivalent to the entire community in virtue and responsibility.

Core Idea
A single truth-bearing scholar can embody the whole community.

This short passage from Sufyan al-Thawri, a great early scholar, encapsulates a profound idea: that the value of a true scholar is not measured by numbers but by the truth he upholds. The author explains this statement by linking it to the Quranic description of Prophet Ibrahim as a 'nation' in himself. This lesson will unpack the meaning and significance of this teaching.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic and translation to grasp the statement and its explanation.
Notice the simple but powerful phrasing.
2
Understand the explanation
The author explains why a single jurist can be considered the community: because he fulfills the community's duties.
This is not literal but metaphorical in terms of value.
3
Connect to Quranic precedent
The verse about Ibrahim shows that an individual can be a whole community in virtue.
Consider how this elevates the status of truthful scholars.

Source Text

وعن سفيان رضي الله عنه: «لو أن فقيها واحدا على رأس جبل لكان هو الجماعة». ومعناه أنه حيث قام بما قام به الجماعة فكأنه جماعة. ومنه قوله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّ إِبْرَاهِيمَ كَانَ أُمَّةً ﴾ [النحل:١٢٠] أي وحده. وقد قيل: وليس على الله بمستنكر أن يجمع العالم في واحد

Its meaning is that when he fulfills what the community fulfills, he is as if he is the community. And from this is the saying of the Almighty: 'Indeed, Ibrahim was a nation' (16:120), meaning alone. And it has been said: And it is not inconceivable for Allah to gather the world in one [person].

Commentary
This passage presents and explains a saying of Sufyan al-Thawri that a single faqih (jurist) who is alone on a mountain is considered the community (jama'a). The author explains that this is because he fulfills the responsibilities that the community would normally fulfill. The Quranic verse about Ibrahim being an 'umma' (nation) is cited as evidence. Finally, a line of poetry reinforces that Allah can gather all virtue in one person.

Al-Ghazali's Classification of the Ruling on Kalam
Al-Ghazali classifies the ruling on kalam with extreme views and the prohibition view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Ghazali's nuanced classification of the ruling on kalam as presented in Ihya' Ulum al-Din, including the extreme views and the authority of the prohibition view among early imams.

Core Idea
Kalam's ruling is contested: some see it as forbidden, others as the best devotion.

Al-Ghazali, in his monumental work Ihya' Ulum al-Din, addresses the controversial status of kalam (theology) and dialectical disputation. He presents the range of opinions from absolute prohibition to recommendation and then notes the authority of the prohibition view held by many early imams. This lesson unpacks his discussion.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Question
Al-Ghazali frames the issue: Is kalam blameworthy like astrology, permissible, or recommended? Recognize the three categories he sets up.
This question defines the scope of the discussion.
2
Contrast the Extreme Views
Note that some consider kalam a forbidden innovation worse than major sins, while others consider it an obligation (fard kifaya or 'ayn) and the best of acts, as it realizes tawhid and defends the religion.
These are the two poles of the debate.
3
Identify the Prohibition Proponents
Al-Ghazali lists major imams who held kalam as prohibited: al-Shafi'i, Muhammad al-Shaybani, Malik, Ahmad, Sufyan al-Thawri, and all hadith imams among the Salaf. Their proof: the Companions' silence despite their eloquence implies harmful consequences.
This anchors the prohibition view in early authority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد فصل الإمام حجة الإسلام" في "إحياء العلوم" هذا المرام حيث قال: «فإن قلت: فعلم الجدل والكلام مذموم كعلم النجوم أو هو مباح أو مندوب ؟ فاعلم أن للناس في هذا غلوّا وإسرافاً في أطراف فمن قائل: إنه بدعة وحرام وإن العبد أن يلقى الله بكل ذنب سوى الشرك له من أن يلقاه بالكلام ومن قائل: إنه ،فرض إما على الكفاية وإما على الأعيان، وإنه أفضل العبادات وأكمل القربات، فإنه تحقيق لعلم التوحيد ونضال عن دين الله المجيد». قال: «وإلى التحريم ذهب الشافعي ومحمد ومالك وأحمد بن حنبل وسفيان وجميع أئمة الحديث من السلف رضي الله عنهم هؤلاء، وأنهم قالوا: «ما سكت عنه عن الصحابة مع أنهم أعرف بالحقائق وأفصح في ترتيب الألفاظ من سائر الخلائق إلا لما يتولد منه ...
And the Proof of Islam (al-Ghazali) detailed this point in 'Ihya' Ulum al-Din' where he said: 'If you say: Is the science of dialectical theology (jadal and kalam) blameworthy like the science of astrology, or is it permissible or recommended? Know that people have gone to extremes in this: some say it is innovation and forbidden, and that a servant meeting Allah with every sin except shirk is better than meeting Him with kalam; others say it is a collective or individual obligation, and that it is the best of acts and most perfect of devotions, because it is the realization of the science of tawhid and struggle for the glorious religion of Allah.' He [al-Ghazali] said: 'And the view of prohibition was held by al-Shafi'i, Muhammad [ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani], Malik, Ahmad ibn Hanbal, Sufyan [al-Thawri], and all the hadith imams among the Salaf, may Allah be pleased with them all, and that they said: "The Companions remained silent about it, even though they were more knowledgeable of realities and more eloquent in arranging words than all other creatures, except because of what arises from it..."'
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage presents al-Ghazali's nuanced classification of the ruling on kalam from his 'Ihya' Ulum al-Din'. He frames it as a response to the question: is the science of jadal (disputation) and kalam (theology) blameworthy like astrology, or is it permissible (mubah) or recommended (mandub)? He notes that people have gone to extremes: some say it is forbidden innovation (bid'a wa haram) and that meeting Allah with any sin except shirk is better than meeting Him with kalam. Others say it is a communal or individual obligation (fard kifaya or fard 'ayn) and the best of acts, as it is the realization of tawhid and defense of the religion. Al-Ghazali then states that the prohibition view was held by major imams including al-Shafi'i, Muhammad al-Shaybani, Malik, Ahmad, Sufyan al-Thawri, and all hadith imams among the Salaf. Their argument, as quoted, is that the Companions remained silent about kalam despite their greater knowledge and eloquence, implying that it leads to harmful consequences (the sentence is cut off).

Key Terms
جدل
كلام
تحريم
إحياء العلوم
بدعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That al-Ghazali personally held kalam to be forbidden and that this passage represents his own final view.
Correction: Al-Ghazali presents both extreme views and then notes the prohibition view of earlier imams, but the passage does not explicitly state his own conclusion; his overall position is more nuanced.

Checkpoint
According to al-Ghazali, which group held the view that kalam is forbidden?
A) The Mu'tazila
B) The later philosophers
C) Al-Shafi'i, Malik, Ahmad, Sufyan, and all Salafi hadith imams
D) The majority of the community

Key Takeaway
Al-Ghazali presents the debate on kalam's ruling and notes that many early imams prohibited it, based on the Companions' silence about it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you engage in discussions about religion, are you more focused on proving you're right or on ensuring the discussion brings you closer to Allah? How can you check your intention before entering a debate?
?
The Companions, despite their deep knowledge and eloquence, chose silence on kalam. Is there an issue in your life where you should stop arguing and simply act upon what you already know? What's holding you back?
?
Al-Ghazali presents two extreme views on kalam. Do you tend to avoid theological topics altogether, or do you dive into them perhaps excessively? Reflect on a recent religious discussion—was it truly beneficial or did it lead to unnecessary division?

First Reasons for Disapproval of Kalam: Avoiding Destructive Disputation
Two reasons for disapproval of kalam with supporting narrative

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two primary reasons early scholars discouraged kalam: turning away from foundational Islam and the dangers of disputation, as illustrated by Abu Hanifa's stance.

Core Idea
Early scholars warned that kalam often leads away from fundamentals and into harmful argumentation.

This passage from Manah al-Rawdh explains why early luminaries like Abu Hanifa discouraged theological disputation. The author presents two interconnected reasons and reinforces them with a famous story about Abu Hanifa refusing to pray behind two disputants. Let's examine the reasoning and the lesson behind it.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing, then read the literal translation. Let the author's argument come through.
Notice the concise style of the original.
2
Identify the two reasons for disapproval
The passage lists two reasons. The first is turning away from the foundations of Islam (الأصول), the second is that disputation leads to corrupt morals and ruinous states.
Both are general warnings against kalam as practiced by some.
3
Examine the story of Abu Hanifa
Read the anecdote about Abu Hanifa refusing to pray behind two disputants—one affirming the Quran is created, the other denying it. Note his explicit reason: 'Disputation about religion is an innovation.'
This demonstrates the second reason in action.
4
Reflect on the nuance
The prohibition is not on all theological discussion but on disputation that leads to division and corrupt morals. Even if one side is correct, the act of arguing can be blameworthy.
The commentary clarifies that the second man is not condemned for his beliefs but for his method.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإنما صدر هذا كله عنهم لأمور: منها ما فهم مما سبق في أثناء الكلام من أن ذمهم عدولهم عن الأخذ بأصول الإسلام واشتغالهم بما لا يعنيهم في مقام المرام. ومنها: منازعتهم ومجادلتهم ولو كان على الحق لإنجراره غالباً إلى مخاصمتهم المؤدية إلى الأخلاق الفاسدة والأحوال الكاسدة كما بينه حجة الإسلام الغزالي في "الإحياء"، فقد ذكر في "غياث المفتي" عن أبي يوسف أنه لا تجوز الصلاة خلف المتكلم وإن تكلم بحق لأنه مبتدع، ولا تجوز خلف المبتدع. وعرضت هذه الرواية على أستاذي فقال: «تأويله أنه لا يكون غرضه إظهار الحق». والذي قاله أستاذي رأيتُه في "تلخيص" الإمام الزاهدي حيث قال: وكان أبو حنيفة يكره الجدل على سبيل الحق حتى روي عن أبي يوسف رحمه الله أنه قال: كنا جلوساً عند أبي حنيفة إذ دخل عليه جماعة في أيديهم رجلان فقالوا: إن أحد هذين يقول القرآن مخلوق، وهذا ينازعه ويقول: هو غير مخلوق، قال: لا تصلوا خلفهما. فقلت: أما الأول فنعم فإنه لا يقول بقدم القرآن، وأما الآخر فما باله لا يصلى خلفه؟ فقال: إنهما يتنازعان في الدين والمنازعة في الدين بدعة. كذا في "مفتاح السعادة". ولعل وجه ذم الآخر حيث أطلق، فإنه محدث إنزاله وإنه مكتوب في مصاحفنا ومقروء بألسنتنا ومحفوظ في صدورنا.
All of this came from them only for matters. Among them: what is understood from what preceded in the course of speech, that their blame (of them) is their turning away from adhering to the foundations of Islam and their occupying themselves with what does not concern them in the station of the goal. And among them: their quarreling and disputation even if it be upon truth, because it mostly leads to their wrangling, which leads to corrupt morals and ruinous states, as explained by the Proof of Islam al-Ghazali in al-Ihya. He mentioned in Ghayath al-Mufti from Abu Yusuf that it is not permissible to pray behind the mutakallim (theologian), even if he speaks truth, because he is an innovator, and it is not permissible to pray behind an innovator. I presented this narration to my teacher, and he said: 'Its interpretation is that his purpose is not to manifest the truth.' What my teacher said, I saw in the Talkhis of Imam al-Zahidi, where he said: Abu Hanifa disliked disputation even upon the side of truth, until it was narrated from Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him, that he said: We were sitting with Abu Hanifa when a group entered upon them, having two men, and they said: One of these two says the Quran is created, and this one disputes with him and says it is uncreated. He said: 'Do not pray behind either of them.' I said: 'As for the first, yes, for he does not affirm the pre-eternity of the Quran; but as for the other, why should one not pray behind him?' He said: 'They are disputing about religion, and disputation about religion is an innovation.' Thus in Miftah al-Sa'ada. And perhaps the reason for blaming the other is that he made an absolute statement, for he is a muhdith (one who speaks of originated matters) regarding its revelation, and it is written in our copies, recited with our tongues, and preserved in our hearts.
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage presents two reasons for the early scholars' disapproval of kalam. The first reason is that the blame of the salaf (early scholars) arose from their observation that those engaged in kalam turned away from the foundational principles of Islam and busied themselves with matters that did not concern them in their religious journey. The second reason is that disputation and argumentation, even when on truth, tend to slide into wrangling and personal confrontation, corrupting morals and ruining spiritual states. The author cites al-Ghazali's Ihya to support this, and reports from Abu Yusuf that it is not permissible to pray behind a mutakallim (theologian) even if he speaks truth, because he is considered an innovator. The author then mentions that he presented this narration to his teacher, who interpreted it to mean that such a person's purpose is not to manifest truth. The author found the same interpretation in al-Zahidi's Talkhis, which includes a story from Abu Yusuf: while sitting with Abu Hanifa, two men were brought in, one claiming the Quran is created, the other disputing and saying it is uncreated. Abu Hanifa forbade praying behind both because they were disputing about religion, and disputation about religion is innovation. The author adds his own explanation that the second man is blameworthy because he made an absolute statement about the Quran being revealed (uncreated) while it is a matter of inference, and the Quran is written, recited, and preserved—referring to the attributes of the Quran. This shows the extreme caution of the early scholars against any form of religious argumentation.

Key Terms
المتكلم
المبتدع
الجدل
المنازعة في الدين
بدعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that early scholars prohibited all theological discussion, including sound reasoning about faith.
Correction: The passage shows that the prohibition is specifically against disputation (جدال) that leads to distraction from fundamentals and corrupt morals, even if the topic is truth. Sound theological reasoning based on Quran and Sunnah was not condemned.

Checkpoint
Why did Abu Hanifa refuse to allow praying behind either of the two disputing men?
A) Because one of them claimed the Quran is created.
B) Because both were engaging in disputation about religion, which is an innovation.
C) Because the second man denied the Quran's pre-eternity.
D) Because they were not practicing Muslims.

Key Takeaway
Disputation about religion, even when on truth, is condemned because it often leads to corrupt morals and innovation, as shown by Abu Hanifa's explicit statement.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you discuss religious topics, do you catch yourself more concerned with being right than with manifesting the truth? How can you ensure your intention remains pure even in a debate?
?
Abu Hanifa considered even the one arguing for the truth to be blameworthy because he engaged in disputation. Is there an issue you feel strongly about that you might be willing to let go of the need to argue for the sake of preserving your humility and sincerity?
?
If you were to apply this teaching today, which common religious discussion online would you distance yourself from, knowing that it often leads to corrupt morals and innovation even when your position is correct?

The Nuanced Ruling on Learning Kalam from al-Khulasa
The author quotes a Hanafi jurist's nuanced ruling on when learning kalam is permissible or forbidden.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the layered Hanafi ruling on learning kalam, distinguishing between permissible and forbidden quantities and intentions.

Core Idea
Learning kalam is not inherently forbidden; the intention and extent determine its ruling.

The Hanafi jurist in al-Khulasa provides a nuanced ruling on learning kalam, showing that it is not simply halal or haram. He distinguishes between learning for necessity and beyond, speaking with fairness versus obstinacy, and warns of the extreme danger of entering debates with the intention to silence opponents. This lesson unpacks these distinctions, helping you appreciate the care taken in classical Islamic scholarship regarding theological discourse.

Guided Path
1
Read the full passage from al-Khulasa
Read the Arabic text and its literal translation carefully to see the structure of the ruling. Pay attention to the different scenarios mentioned.
2
Identify the three scenarios
Notice that the ruling covers: (1) learning kalam more than necessary, (2) learning astronomy for prayer times and qibla, and (3) speaking about kalam with different intentions (fairness vs. obstinacy vs. silencing the opponent).
3
Analyze the rulings on each scenario
Determine which actions are permissible, disliked, forbidden, or lead to kufr. The passage uses terms like 'la ba'sa bihi' (no harm), 'haram' (forbidden), 'la yukrah' (not disliked), 'yakfur' (becomes a disbeliever), and 'yukhsha 'alayhi al-kufr' (disbelief is feared for him).
4
Reflect on the underlying principle
Consider why intention and fairness matter so much. The ruling shows that kalam is a tool that can be used for truth or for strife, so the ruling depends on the manner and purpose.
This step connects the specific rulings to broader Islamic ethical principles about intention (niyya) and adab in debate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هذا وفى كتاب "الخلاصة: «تعلم علم الكلام والنظر فيه والمناظرة وراء قدر الحاجة عنه وتعلم علم النجوم قدر ما يعلم به مواقيت الصلاة والقبلة لا بأس به والزيادة حرام، ثم تكلمه على الإنصاف لا يكره بلا تعنت واعتساف، وإن تكلم من يريد التعنت يطرحه لا يكره. قال : وسمعت القاضي الإمام: إن أراد تحجيل الخصم يكفر، قال وعندي لا يكفر ويخشى عليه الكفر، انتهى كلام صاحب "الخلاصة".
And in the book al-Khulasa: 'Learning the science of kalam, looking into it, and debating beyond the amount needed for it, and learning the science of astronomy to the extent by which the times of prayer and the direction of the qibla are known, there is no harm in it, and the increase is forbidden. Then, speaking (about it) with fairness (insaf) is not disliked, without obstinacy (ta'annut) and distortion (i'tisaf). And if one speaks intending obstinacy, it is not disliked that he is repelled. He said: And I heard the Qadi Imam: If he intends to silence the opponent (tahjil al-khasm), he becomes a disbeliever. He said: In my view, he does not become a disbeliever, but disbelief is feared for him. End of the words of the author of al-Khulasa.'
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage presents a nuanced ruling from the Hanafi jurisprudential work al-Khulasa regarding the permissibility of learning kalam. The ruling distinguishes between learning kalam beyond one's need (which is forbidden) and learning it to the necessary extent (which is allowed). It also addresses the teaching of astronomy (ilm al-nujum) for prayer times and qibla direction, which is permissible but not more. For kalam itself, if one speaks with fairness (insaf) and without obstinacy (ta'annut) or distortion (i'tisaf), it is not disliked (makruh). If one speaks with the intention of obstinacy, it is not disliked that he is repelled (i.e., silenced). Then it reports a statement from the Qadi Imam (a title for a Hanafi jurist, perhaps Abu Yusuf or another): if a person intends to 'tahjil al-khasm' (silencing the opponent by flustering him, not seeking truth), he becomes a disbeliever. The author of al-Khulasa adds his own view: he does not become a disbeliever, but disbelief is feared for him. This shows the extreme seriousness of engaging in kalam with the wrong intention.

Key Terms
علم الكلام
القدر الحاجة
الإنصاف
التعنت
تحجيل الخصم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that any form of kalam is absolutely forbidden.
Correction: Al-Khulasa allows it when done with fairness and without obstinacy, and even permits learning the necessary amount.

Checkpoint
According to al-Khulasa, what is the ruling on learning kalam beyond one's need?
A) Permissible.
B) Recommended.
C) Forbidden (haram).
D) Disliked (makruh).

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of learning kalam depends on the amount (need) and the intention (fairness seeking truth vs. obstinacy or silencing opponents).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you engage in religious discussions online or with friends, do you ever catch yourself wanting to 'win' or embarrass the other person? What does this passage teach you about the danger of that intention? What will you do the next time you feel that urge?
?
Are there areas of religious knowledge you pursue beyond what is practically needed—out of curiosity, pride, or desire to debate? How does al-Khulasa's distinction between 'necessary amount' and 'forbidden increase' challenge you to reassess your study habits? What one thing can you cut back on starting today?
?
If your heart were examined right now, would your approach to theological discussion reflect insaf (fairness) or tahjil (silencing)? What hidden motives might be at play? Commit to one concrete action—like listening more before responding—to align your intention with seeking truth.

Warnings from Scholars: The Regret of Engaging in Kalam
Collects regret statements from five scholars about kalam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the serious warnings and regrets expressed by prominent Islamic scholars regarding the dangers of excessive engagement in kalam (speculative theology) without proper guidance.

Core Idea
Even great scholars warned that kalam can lead to confusion and ruinous regret.

This lesson presents firsthand accounts from respected scholars like al-Shahrastani, al-Juwayni, and others who confessed their deep regret over delving into kalam. Their testimonies serve as cautionary tales about the risks of rational speculation divorced from revelation.

Guided Path
1
Read the scholars' statements
Read each scholar's regret carefully, noting the common theme of confusion and remorse.
2
Identify the progression
Notice how the regrets intensify from al-Shahrastani's confusion to al-Juwayni's fear at death, to al-Khusrawshahi's weeping uncertainty.
3
Consider the anonymous scholar
The unnamed scholar's sleepless night weighing proofs shows the persistent doubt that can result from kalam.
4
Reflect on the warning
The passage warns that without divine mercy, such a state can lead to heresy (tazandduq).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذا قال الشهرستاني رحمه الله : إنه لم يجد على الفلاسفة والمتكلمين إلا الحيرة والندم حيث قال : لعمري لقد طفت المعاهد كلها وسيرت طرفي بين تلك المعالم فلم أر إلا واضعاً كف حائر على ذقن أو قارعاً سن نادم وكذا قال أبو المعالي الجويني: يا أصحابنا لا تشتغلوا بالكلام فلو عرفت أن الكلام يبلغ بي إلى ما بلغ ما اشتغلت به. وقال عند موته: لقد خضت البحر الخضم وخليت أهل الإسلام وعلومهم ودخلت في الذي نهوني عنه والآن فإن لم يتداركني ربي برحمته فالويل لابن الجويني وها أنا ذا أموت على عقيدة أمي أو قال على عقيدة عجائز أهل نيسابور. وكذا قال الخسرو شاهي وكان من أجل تلامذة فخر الدين الرازي لبعض الفضلاء ودخل عليه يوما ما تعتقده؟ قال : ما يعتقده المسلمون فقال : وأنت منشرح الصدر لذلك مستيقن به؟ أو كما قال، فقال: نعم، فقال: اشكر الله على هذه النعمة، ولكني والله ما أدري ما أعتقد، بكى حتى أخضل لحيته. وقال الخونجي عند موته ما عرفت مما حصلته شيئا سوى أن الممكن مفتقر إلى المرجح ، ثم قال : الافتقار وصف سلبي، أموت وما عرفت شيئاً. وقال آخر: أضطجع على فراشي وأضع الملحفة على وجهي وأقابل بين حجج هؤلاء وهؤلاء حتى يطلع الفجر ولم يترجح عندي منها شيء، ومن يصل إلى مثل هذا الحال إن لم يتداركه الله بالرحمة والإقبال تزندق وساء له المآل؛ فالدواء النافع لمثل هذا المرض ما كان طبيب القلوب يتضرع به إلى علام الغيوب ويدعو بقوله: اللهم يا مقلب القلوب ثبت قلبي على دينك. وبقوله: اللهم فاطر السموات والأرض عالم الغيب والشهادة اهدني لما اختلفوا فيه من الحق بإذنك إنك تهدي من تشاء إلى صراط مستقيم. وبقوله: لا حول ولا قوة إلا بالله العلي العظيم.
And likewise al-Shahrastani said, may Allah have mercy on him: He found nothing but confusion and regret upon the philosophers and theologians, where he said: By my life, I have toured all the institutes and directed my sight among those landmarks, and I saw nothing but one placing a hand of confusion on a chin or one gnashing a tooth of regret. And likewise Abu al-Ma'ali al-Juwayni said: O our companions, do not occupy yourselves with kalam, for if I had known that kalam would lead me to what it has led, I would not have occupied myself with it. And he said at his death: I have plunged into the deep sea and left the people of Islam and their sciences, and I entered into that which they forbade me, and now if my Lord does not take care of me with His mercy, then woe to Ibn al-Juwayni, and here I am dying upon the creed of my mother, or he said: upon the creed of the old women of Nishapur. And likewise al-Khusrawshahi, who was among the greatest students of Fakhr al-Din al-Razi, said to some virtuous man who entered upon him one day: What do you believe? He said: What the Muslims believe. He said: And are you at ease with that and certain of it? or as he said. He said: Yes. He said: Thank Allah for this blessing, but by Allah I do not know what I believe. He wept until his beard became wet. And al-Khunji said at his death: I have not known from what I have acquired anything except that the contingent is in need of a preponderator. Then he said: Need is a negative attribute. I die and have known nothing. And another said: I lie on my bed and place the blanket over my face and compare the proofs of these and these until dawn breaks, and nothing becomes preponderant with me from them. And whoever reaches such a state, if Allah does not take care of him with mercy and acceptance, he will become a heretic and his end will be evil. So the beneficial cure for such a disease is what the physician of hearts supplicates with to the Knower of the Unseen, and he calls upon Him with His saying: O Allah, O Turner of hearts, make my heart firm upon Your religion. And with His saying: O Allah, Originator of the heavens and the earth, Knower of the unseen and the witnessed, guide me to that which they have differed about of the truth by Your permission, indeed You guide whom You will to a straight path. And with His saying: There is no power and no strength except with Allah, the Most High, the Almighty.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage collects cautionary statements from several prominent scholars regarding the dangers of engaging in kalam (speculative theology) without proper grounding. It begins with al-Shahrastani, who found only confusion (ḥayra) and regret (nadam) among philosophers and theologians. Then al-Juwayni (Imam al-Haramayn) warns his companions not to occupy themselves with kalam, expressing that if he had known where it would lead him, he would not have started. At his death, he expresses fear of ending up on the simple faith of his mother or old women, implying that excessive speculation led him away from simple belief. Next, al-Khusrawshahi, a student of Fakhr al-Din al-Razi, confesses his uncertainty, weeping because he does not know what he truly believes despite outwardly following Muslims. Al-Khunji admits he only learned that the contingent needs a preponderator, but then notes that need is a negative attribute, leading to despair. Another anonymous scholar describes sleepless nights weighing proofs without resolution, warning that without divine mercy such a state leads to heresy (tazandduq). The author then provides the remedy: heartfelt supplications from the Prophet’s traditions, asking Allah to keep the heart firm on the religion, to guide to truth amid differences, and to affirm that all power is from Allah. This passage illustrates the risk of losing simple faith through excessive rational speculation and emphasizes the importance of divine guidance.

Key Terms
حيرة
ندم
كلام
عقيدة عجائز
ممكن
مرجح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The scholars' regret means kalam is entirely forbidden and useless.
Correction: Their regret is about improper kalam that leads to doubt, not about kalam done with proper methodology and reliance on revelation.

Checkpoint
According to al-Juwayni, what did he say about his engagement with kalam?
A) He praised it as the best science.
B) He regretted it and wished he had not started.
C) He said it was obligatory for all Muslims.
D) He claimed it led him to certainty.

Key Takeaway
Great Islamic scholars warned that without divine guidance, kalam can lead to confusion, regret, and even heresy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever pursued knowledge that left you more confused or further from certainty? What will you do to avoid the regret of al-Juwayni, who wished he had stayed with the simple faith of his mother?
?
Al-Khusrawshahi wept because he could not say what he truly believed. Do you know what you believe with certainty, or are you relying on inherited faith? Will you seek personal conviction before it is too late?
?
The anonymous scholar compared proofs all night without reaching resolution. Are you willing to risk your faith by engaging in debates that may lead you to heresy? What concrete step will you take today to secure your belief in Allah's mercy?

The Remedy for Theological Confusion: Supplication as Cure
Prescribes three prophetic supplications as remedy for confusion from kalam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will learn the prophetic supplications prescribed as a remedy for the confusion and doubt that can arise from kalam.

Core Idea
The cure for theological confusion is humble supplication to Allah, not more argumentation.

After presenting the regrets of scholars, the author prescribes a cure: turning to Allah in supplication. This lesson presents three specific prophetic du'as that seek firmness of heart, guidance amid differences, and reliance on divine strength.

Guided Path
1
Read the cure introduction
Notice how the author describes the remedy as what the 'physician of hearts' (the Prophet) supplicates with.
2
Learn the first du'a
The Prophet asked Allah to keep his heart firm on the religion.
3
Learn the second du'a
The Prophet asked Allah to guide him to truth in matters of disagreement.
4
Learn the third du'a
The Prophet affirmed that all power and strength come from Allah alone.
5
Reflect on the approach
Contrast the method of engaging in endless debate with the method of humble supplication.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

A) اللهم اغفر لي

The final remedy for confusion in matters of faith is turning to Allah in humble supplication, not continuing endless debate.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter uncertainty about your faith, do you immediately resort to more research and debate, or do you humbly cry out to Allah with these very du'as? Will you make the du'a 'O Turner of hearts' your first response today?
?
The Prophet ﷺ himself used these three du'as as the ultimate cure for confusion. Are you willing to memorize them and incorporate them into your daily prayers, trusting that Allah alone can guide your heart, no matter how strong your reasoning?
?
Which of these three du'as do you most need to internalize right now: steadfastness, guidance amidst differing opinions, or utter reliance on Allah's power? Are you ready to bow your rational pride and plead with Allah using these words, starting tonight in your sujood?

Using Pure Reason in Fiqh and Tawhid is Innovation
First argument: reason in fiqh and tawhid is innovation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why classical Sunni scholars considered using pure reason without revelation in fiqh and tawhid to be innovation and misguidance.

Core Idea
Reason cannot be a legal cause without divine revelation.

The passage begins by asserting that relying on opinion and pure reason in jurisprudence and sharia is innovation and misguidance. This is even more emphatically true for the sciences of divine unity and attributes. The author supports this with a quote from the Hanafi jurist al-Bazdawi, who explains that reason cannot function as a cause or legal ground apart from the Lawgiver. Let's examine this argument closely.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice the strong language: 'innovation and misguidance' is used for both fiqh and tawhid.
The passage uses the phrase 'فأولى' (so more fitting) to strengthen the point.
2
Identify the claim about reason
The passage claims that using pure reason (العقل المجرد) and opinion (الرأي) in fiqh is already a serious error. Identify the quote from al-Bazdawi that supports this.
Al-Bazdawi's statement: 'لم يرد في الشرع دليل على أن العقل موجب ولا يجوز أن يكون موجبا وعلة بدون الشرع'.
3
Understand the reasoning behind the prohibition
Al-Bazdawi argues that legal grounds (علل) are set only by the Lawgiver. Reason cannot be a cause without textual evidence. Making reason independent leads to partnership (الشركة) with Allah in legislation.
The term 'الشركة' here refers to associating oneself with Allah in a role that belongs only to Him.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider how this argument applies to theology (tawhid). If reason cannot be a cause in legal matters, it certainly cannot dictate matters of divine attributes. The author insists this is even more severe.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها: أن القول بالرأي والعقل المجرد في الفقه والشريعة بدعة وضلالة فأولى أن يكون ذلك في علم التوحيد والصفات بدعة وضلالة، فقد قال فخر الإسلام علي البزدوي في أصول الفقه: إنه لم يرد في الشرع دليل على أن العقل موجب ولا يجوز أن يكون موجبا وعلة بدون الشرع، إذ العلل موضوعات الشرع، وليس إلى العباد ذلك؛ لأنه ينزع أي يسوق إلى الشركة، فمن جعله موجبا بلا دليل شرعا فقد جاوز حد العباد وتعدى عن حد الشرع على وجه العناد. ومنها: الإصغاء إلى كلام الحكماء وأتباعهم من السفهاء حيث أعرضوا عن الآيات النازلة السماء وخاضوا مع الجهلاء الذين يظن فيهم أنهم العقلاء والعلماء وقد نبه الله تعالى على ذلك في كتابه حيث قال: ﴿وَإِذَا رَأَيْتَ الَّذِينَ يَخُوضُونَ فِي آيَاتِنَا فَأَعْرِضْ عَنْهُمْ حَتَّى يَخُوضُوا فِي حَدِيثٍ غَيْرِهِ﴾ [الأنعام: 68] فإن معنى الآية يشملهم إذ العبرة بعموم المبنى لا بخصوص السبب لذلك المعنى، والتأويلات الباطلة والتحريفات العاطلة قد تكون كفراً وقد تكون فسقاً وقد تكون معصية وقد تكون خطأ والخطأ في هذا الباب غير معفو ومرفوع بخلاف الخطأ في اجتهاد الفروع حيث لا وزر هنالك بل أجر يترتب على ذلك. وبهذا تبين وجه الفرق بين اجتهاد أهل البدعة مع اختلافهم وبين اجتهاد أهل السنة مع اختلافهم ويشير إليه قوله تعالى: يُضِلُّ بِهِ كَثِيرًا وَيَهْدِي بِهِ كَثِيرًا [البقرة: 26] وَنُنَزِّلُ مِنَ الْقُرْآنِ مَا هُوَ شِفَاءٌ وَرَحْمَةٌ لِلْمُؤْمِنِينَ وَلَا يَزِيدُ الظَّالِمِينَ إِلَّا خَسَارًا [الإسراء: 82] وفي الحديث: القرآن حجة
And among them: That opinion and pure reason in jurisprudence and sharia is innovation and misguidance, so it is more fitting that this be innovation and misguidance in the science of divine unity and attributes. For Fakhr al-Islam Ali al-Bazdawi said in Usul al-Fiqh: No evidence has come in the law that reason is a cause, nor is it permissible for it to be a cause and a legal ground without the law, for legal grounds are subject matters of the law, and the servants have no authority over that; because it leads to partnership. So whoever makes it a cause without legal evidence has exceeded the bounds of servants and transgressed the limits of the law out of obstinacy. And among them: Listening to the speech of the philosophers and their followers from the foolish, who have turned away from the verses sent down from heaven and plunged with the ignorant who are thought to be the intelligent and the learned. Allah the Exalted has pointed this out in His Book when He said: {And when you see those who engage in false discourse concerning Our verses, turn away from them until they engage in another discourse} [Al-An'am: 68]. Indeed the meaning of the verse includes them, for consideration is by the generality of the wording not by the particularity of the occasion. And the false interpretations and corrupt distortions may be disbelief, or may be disobedience, or may be sin, or may be error. And error in this chapter is not excused or raised, unlike error in the ijtihad of subsidiary matters where there is no sin there, rather reward is attached to that. And by this the distinction becomes clear between the ijtihad of the people of innovation with their differences and the ijtihad of the people of the Sunnah with their differences. And to it points His saying: {He misleads many thereby and guides many thereby} [Al-Baqarah: 26] and {And We send down of the Quran that which is a healing and a mercy for the believers, and it does not increase the wrongdoers except loss} [Al-Isra: 82]. And in the hadith: The Quran is a proof...
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage presents two key arguments against reliance on reason independent of revelation in matters of faith and law. First, it argues that using opinion and pure reason in fiqh (jurisprudence) and sharia is innovation (bid'a) and misguidance, and it is even more so in the science of tawhid (divine unity) and divine attributes. The author quotes al-Bazdawi, who states that reason cannot be a legal cause (mu'ajjib) without textual evidence, as legal grounds are established by the Lawgiver alone. Making reason an independent cause leads to shirk (association) and transgresses the bounds of servitude. Second, the passage warns against listening to philosophers (hukama') and their followers, who turn away from revealed verses. The Quranic verse (al-An'am 6:68) commands turning away from those who engage in false discourse about Allah's signs, and this applies to all such people, as the general wording is considered, not the specific occasion. The author then distinguishes between error in principles (usul) and error in subsidiary matters (furu'). Error in principles—like false interpretations and distortions—can be disbelief, sin, etc., and is not excused, whereas error in ijtihad in subsidiary rulings carries no sin but rather reward. This clarifies the difference between the ijtihad of innovators and that of Ahl al-Sunna. The passage concludes with Quranic verses illustrating that the same Quran guides some and misleads others, and that it is healing for believers but increases loss for wrongdoers, and a hadith stating the Quran is a proof.

Key Terms
رأي
عقل مجرد
بدعة
ضلالة
موجب
علة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Reason can independently determine right and wrong in religious matters without revelation.
Correction: The passage asserts that reason cannot be a legal cause (موجب) nor a ground (علة) without scriptural evidence; doing so leads to innovation and shirk.

Checkpoint
According to al-Bazdawi as quoted, what happens if someone makes reason a cause (موجب) without scriptural evidence?
A) He earns reward for ijtihad.
B) He exceeds the bounds of servants and transgresses the limits of the law.
C) He is considered a philosopher.
D) He commits a minor sin.

Key Takeaway
Reason cannot be an independent source of legislation or theology; it must be guided by revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever find yourself relying on your own reasoning in matters of faith, even when you know the revealed texts point differently? What specific area of belief or practice might that be?
?
If using reason in theology is a transgression that leads to 'partnership' with Allah, how seriously do you take the danger of intellectual independence in religious matters? What step will you take this week to ensure your reasoning is guided by revelation first?
?
When you encounter a theological question not directly addressed in scripture, what is your immediate impulse – to reason it out or to seek guidance from the scholars of the Salaf? Which path will you choose tomorrow when a doubt arises?

Warning Against Philosophers and Error in Principles vs. Subsidiaries
Second argument: warning against philosophers and error in usul vs furu'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between error in principles of faith (usul) and subsidiary matters (furu'), and why the former is not excused.

Core Idea
Error in theological principles is not excused, unlike error in subsidiary ijtihad.

The second argument warns against listening to philosophers who turn away from Quranic verses. It then cites a verse commanding to turn away from those who engage in false discourse. The author explains that such false interpretations can be disbelief, sin, or error, but error in principles is not excused—unlike error in ijtihad in subsidiary rulings. This distinction clarifies the difference between the ijtihad of innovators and that of Ahl al-Sunna.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the warning against philosophers (الحكماء) and their followers.
The term 'الحكماء' often refers to Greek-influenced philosophers.
2
Understand the Quranic verse and its application
The verse (Al-An'am 6:68) commands turning away from those who engage in false discourse about Allah's verses. The author says this applies generally, not just to the specific occasion of revelation.
The principle: 'العبرة بعموم المبنى لا بخصوص السبب'.
3
Distinguish error in usul vs furu'
Errors in interpreting foundational texts (تأويلات باطلة) can range from disbelief to sin. Importantly, such errors are not excused (غير معفو). In contrast, error in ijtihad in subsidiary matters (فروع) carries no sin but reward.
This is a key distinction: in principles, the standard is stricter.
4
See how Quranic verses illustrate the point
The passage ends with two Quranic verses showing that the same Quran guides some and misleads others, and a hadith that the Quran is a proof. Reflect on how this supports the distinction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها: أن القول بالرأي والعقل المجرد في الفقه والشريعة بدعة وضلالة فأولى أن يكون ذلك في علم التوحيد والصفات بدعة وضلالة، فقد قال فخر الإسلام علي البزدوي في أصول الفقه: إنه لم يرد في الشرع دليل على أن العقل موجب ولا يجوز أن يكون موجبا وعلة بدون الشرع، إذ العلل موضوعات الشرع، وليس إلى العباد ذلك؛ لأنه ينزع أي يسوق إلى الشركة، فمن جعله موجبا بلا دليل شرعا فقد جاوز حد العباد وتعدى عن حد الشرع على وجه العناد. ومنها: الإصغاء إلى كلام الحكماء وأتباعهم من السفهاء حيث أعرضوا عن الآيات النازلة السماء وخاضوا مع الجهلاء الذين يظن فيهم أنهم العقلاء والعلماء وقد نبه الله تعالى على ذلك في كتابه حيث قال: ﴿وَإِذَا رَأَيْتَ الَّذِينَ يَخُوضُونَ فِي آيَاتِنَا فَأَعْرِضْ عَنْهُمْ حَتَّى يَخُوضُوا فِي حَدِيثٍ غَيْرِهِ﴾ [الأنعام: 68] فإن معنى الآية يشملهم إذ العبرة بعموم المبنى لا بخصوص السبب لذلك المعنى، والتأويلات الباطلة والتحريفات العاطلة قد تكون كفراً وقد تكون فسقاً وقد تكون معصية وقد تكون خطأ والخطأ في هذا الباب غير معفو ومرفوع بخلاف الخطأ في اجتهاد الفروع حيث لا وزر هنالك بل أجر يترتب على ذلك. وبهذا تبين وجه الفرق بين اجتهاد أهل البدعة مع اختلافهم وبين اجتهاد أهل السنة مع اختلافهم ويشير إليه قوله تعالى: يُضِلُّ بِهِ كَثِيرًا وَيَهْدِي بِهِ كَثِيرًا [البقرة: 26] وَنُنَزِّلُ مِنَ الْقُرْآنِ مَا هُوَ شِفَاءٌ وَرَحْمَةٌ لِلْمُؤْمِنِينَ وَلَا يَزِيدُ الظَّالِمِينَ إِلَّا خَسَارًا [الإسراء: 82] وفي الحديث: القرآن حجة
And among them: That opinion and pure reason in jurisprudence and sharia is innovation and misguidance, so it is more fitting that this be innovation and misguidance in the science of divine unity and attributes. For Fakhr al-Islam Ali al-Bazdawi said in Usul al-Fiqh: No evidence has come in the law that reason is a cause, nor is it permissible for it to be a cause and a legal ground without the law, for legal grounds are subject matters of the law, and the servants have no authority over that; because it leads to partnership. So whoever makes it a cause without legal evidence has exceeded the bounds of servants and transgressed the limits of the law out of obstinacy. And among them: Listening to the speech of the philosophers and their followers from the foolish, who have turned away from the verses sent down from heaven and plunged with the ignorant who are thought to be the intelligent and the learned. Allah the Exalted has pointed this out in His Book when He said: {And when you see those who engage in false discourse concerning Our verses, turn away from them until they engage in another discourse} [Al-An'am: 68]. Indeed the meaning of the verse includes them, for consideration is by the generality of the wording not by the particularity of the occasion. And the false interpretations and corrupt distortions may be disbelief, or may be disobedience, or may be sin, or may be error. And error in this chapter is not excused or raised, unlike error in the ijtihad of subsidiary matters where there is no sin there, rather reward is attached to that. And by this the distinction becomes clear between the ijtihad of the people of innovation with their differences and the ijtihad of the people of the Sunnah with their differences. And to it points His saying: {He misleads many thereby and guides many thereby} [Al-Baqarah: 26] and {And We send down of the Quran that which is a healing and a mercy for the believers, and it does not increase the wrongdoers except loss} [Al-Isra: 82]. And in the hadith: The Quran is a proof...
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage presents two key arguments against reliance on reason independent of revelation in matters of faith and law. First, it argues that using opinion and pure reason in fiqh (jurisprudence) and sharia is innovation (bid'a) and misguidance, and it is even more so in the science of tawhid (divine unity) and divine attributes. The author quotes al-Bazdawi, who states that reason cannot be a legal cause (mu'ajjib) without textual evidence, as legal grounds are established by the Lawgiver alone. Making reason an independent cause leads to shirk (association) and transgresses the bounds of servitude. Second, the passage warns against listening to philosophers (hukama') and their followers, who turn away from revealed verses. The Quranic verse (al-An'am 6:68) commands turning away from those who engage in false discourse about Allah's signs, and this applies to all such people, as the general wording is considered, not the specific occasion. The author then distinguishes between error in principles (usul) and error in subsidiary matters (furu'). Error in principles—like false interpretations and distortions—can be disbelief, sin, etc., and is not excused, whereas error in ijtihad in subsidiary rulings carries no sin but rather reward. This clarifies the difference between the ijtihad of innovators and that of Ahl al-Sunna. The passage concludes with Quranic verses illustrating that the same Quran guides some and misleads others, and that it is healing for believers but increases loss for wrongdoers, and a hadith stating the Quran is a proof.

تأويل

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All errors in religious understanding are equally forgivable.
Correction: The passage distinguishes error in principles (usul) from error in subsidiary ijtihad (furu'); the former is not excused, while the latter may be rewarded.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on error in ijtihad in subsidiary matters (furu')?
A) It is never excused and incurs sin.
B) It is excused and the mujtahid receives reward.
C) It leads to disbelief.
D) It is equivalent to error in principles.

Key Takeaway
Error in foundational theological principles is not excused, while error in sincere ijtihad in subsidiary rulings is rewarded.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the Quran, do you find yourself seeking to understand it as the Salaf understood it, or do you try to make it fit your own opinions and desires? The warning against philosophers is a warning against subjecting revelation to human reasoning. Have you ever prioritized your intellect over a clear verse? If so, what will you do to correct that today?
?
You have likely disagreed with a scholar or fellow Muslim on a minor issue of fiqh. Did you respect their ijtihad and consider their error rewarded, or did you secretly judge them as misguided? The lesson teaches that error in subsidiary matters is not only excused but rewarded. Can you truly accept that in your heart, or do you still harbor resentment? Commit now to treating such differences with Islamic brotherhood.
?
The Quran increases the wrongdoers only in loss. This is a terrifying reality. When you open the Quran, what is your intention? Do you read it to be guided, or to find proof for your own preferences? Examine your heart honestly. If you are using the Quran to justify your own desires, you are in grave danger. Make a firm resolve from this moment to approach the Quran with humility and submission, seeking only the truth.
